decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Map_of_Dublin_Airport.png/330px-Map_of_Dublin_Airport.png 1.5x, class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Dublin_Airport.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Dublin Airport (before the construction of runway 10L/28R)</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Dublin Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga"><b>Aerfort Bhaile \xc3\x81tha Cliath</b></i>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>DUB</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EIDW</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> serving <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, Ireland. It is operated by <a href="/wiki/DAA_(Irish_company)" title="DAA (Irish company)">DAA</a> (formerly Dublin Airport Authority).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The airport is located 7&#160;km (4.3&#160;mi) north<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, in Collinstown, and 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) south of the town of <a href="/wiki/Swords,_Dublin" title="Swords, Dublin">Swords</a>.\n</p><p>In 2019, 32.9 million passengers passed through the airport, making it the airport\'s busiest year on record.<sup id="cite_ref-2019numbersRTE_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019numbersRTE-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">12th busiest airport in Europe</a>, and is by far the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="List of the busiest airports in the Republic of Ireland">busiest of Ireland\'s airports by total passenger traffic</a>; it also has the greatest traffic levels on the <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">island of Ireland</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a>.\n</p><p>The airport has an extensive <a href="/wiki/Flight_length" title="Flight length">short and medium haul</a> network, served by an array of carriers, as well as a significant long-haul network focused on <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. It serves as the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, regional airline <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ASL_Airlines_Ireland" title="ASL Airlines Ireland">ASL Airlines Ireland</a>, together with another two airlines, <a href="/wiki/CityJet" title="CityJet">CityJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_International" title="Norwegian Air International">Norwegian Air International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_States_border_preclearance" title="United States border preclearance">United States border preclearance</a> services are available at the airport for U.S.-bound passengers. <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon Airport</a> is the only other airport in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> to offer this facility.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collinstown_Aerodrome">Collinstown Aerodrome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Collinstown Aerodrome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1917, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>,  the <a href="/wiki/Townland" title="Townland">townland</a> of <a href="/wiki/Collinstown,_Santry" title="Collinstown, Santry">Collinstown</a> was selected as the site of a base for the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">Royal Flying Corps</a>. By April 1918, when the Flying Corps was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, <b>Collinstown Aerodrome</b> was more than 20% complete. Construction was completed in 1919 when the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Irish War of Independence</a> broke out. On 20 March 1919 a group of 30 <a href="/wiki/Irish_Volunteer" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Volunteer">Irish Volunteers</a>, including five employed by the RAF, stole 75 rifles and 5,000 rounds of ammunition from the base.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>  As <b>Collinstown Camp</b> the site was used for <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">internment</a> of Irish republicans.<sup id="cite_ref-McGarry2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGarry2015-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 1922 the land and buildings at Collinstown were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>. The airfield quickly fell into disrepair and grass grew on the former runways.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_beginnings_in_the_1930s_and_1940s">The beginnings in the 1930s and 1940s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The beginnings in the 1930s and 1940s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg/220px-Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg/330px-Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg/440px-Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_1940_terminal_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original <a href="/wiki/International_style_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="International style (architecture)">international style</a> passenger terminal, completed in 1940</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Executive Council of the Irish Free State">Executive Council of the Irish Free State</a> established a new civil airline, <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, which began operating from the <a href="/wiki/Military_airbase" class="mw-redirect" title="Military airbase">military aerodrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casement_Aerodrome" title="Casement Aerodrome">Casement Aerodrome</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Baldonnel,_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Baldonnel, Ireland">Baldonnel</a> to the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. A decision was made that a civil airport should replace Baldonnel as Dublin\'s airport.  The former Collinstown site, extended into the neighbouring townlands of Rock and Corballis, was chosen.\n</p><p>Work on the new airport began in 1937. By the end of 1939, a grass airfield surface, internal roads, car parks and electrical power and lighting were set up. The inaugural flight from Dublin took place on 19 January 1940 to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>. In August 1938, work began on a new <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">airport terminal</a> building. The terminal building was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Desmond_FitzGerald_(architect)" title="Desmond FitzGerald (architect)">Desmond FitzGerald</a>, brother of politician <a href="/wiki/Garret_FitzGerald" title="Garret FitzGerald">Garret FitzGerald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> FitzGerald, who had designed an airport terminal as part of his college studies, led a team of architects that also included Kevin Barry, Daith\xc3\xad Hanley, Charles Aliaga Kelly, Dermot O\'Toole and Harry Robson. The terminal building opened in early 1941, with its design heavily influenced by the tiered structure of the luxury ocean liners of the time. The terminal was awarded the Triennial Gold Medal of the Royal Hibernian Institute of Architects in 1942 and is today a listed building.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_(5997469039).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg/220px-Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg/330px-Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg/440px-Dublin_Airport_%285997469039%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="827" data-file-height="510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_(5997469039).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> <a href="/wiki/DC-3" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-3">DC-3</a> plane at Dublin Airport\'s original Terminal 1 in May 1950.</div></div></div>\n<p>Due to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, which was known as <a href="/wiki/The_Emergency_(Ireland)" title="The Emergency (Ireland)">The Emergency</a> in Ireland, services were severely restricted at Dublin Airport until late 1945. The only international scheduled routes operated during this time were by Aer Lingus to Liverpool (and for a period to <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/City_Airport_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="City Airport Manchester">Barton Aerodrome</a>). The end of the war meant the beginning of a major expansion in services at the airport. Aer Lingus resumed its London service to Croydon in November 1945. In 1947, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> started the first European flights to Dublin with a service to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>. Three new concrete runways were completed in 1948, and in 1950 - after ten years in operation - the airport had welcomed a total of 920,000 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-dublinairport.com_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dublinairport.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Expanding_in_the_1950s.2C_1960s_and_1970s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Expanding_in_the_1950s,_1960s_and_1970s">Expanding in the 1950s, 1960s and 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Expanding in the 1950s, 1960s and 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Throughout the 1950s Dublin Airport expanded with virtually uninterrupted traffic growth. Runway extensions and terminal enhancements were carried out to deal with the influx of traffic and passengers. New airlines began serving the airport also. These included <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Airlines_(UK)" title="Northeast Airlines (UK)">BKS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80s&amp;90s_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80s&amp;90s-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1958, a new transatlantic service was started by Aer Lingus via <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon Airport</a>. By the mid 1950s, it was clear that the original terminal building was too small to cope with growing passenger numbers. A new North Terminal was opened in June 1959. Originally, the plan was that North Terminal would handle all US and European flights, but instead, it became the arrivals terminal for all Dublin Airport passengers, while the original passenger terminal was used for departures.<sup id="cite_ref-dublinairport.com_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dublinairport.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1960s, the number of scheduled carriers continued to grow. By the close of the 1960s, a sizeable number of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737s</a>, <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Elevens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Trident" title="Hawker Siddeley Trident">Hawker Siddeley Tridents</a> were using the airport regularly. To cope with larger aircraft in the late 1960s new departure gate piers were added close to the old terminal to cope with larger aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-dublinairport.com_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dublinairport.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> These piers would subsequently be connected to Terminal 1. During 1969, the airport handled 1,737,151 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-80s&amp;90s_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80s&amp;90s-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The advent of <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> posed opportunities and challenges for aviation. In 1971, Aer Lingus took delivery of two new Boeing 747 aircraft; the first one arrived in March and, shortly afterwards, performed a flyover above <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Street" title="O&#39;Connell Street">O\'Connell Street</a> in Dublin on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Day">Saint Patrick\'s Day</a>; a third <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> was delivered later that decade. To cope with this, a new \xc2\xa310 million passenger terminal capable of handling six million passengers per year, which became known as Terminal 1, was opened in June 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-dublinairport.com_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dublinairport.com-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The growth which was anticipated at Dublin\'s airport (and provided for through heavy investment by the airport and Aer Lingus) during the 1970s did not materialise immediately.\n</p><p>On 30 November 1975, one person was killed and eight others were injured when the airport <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport_bombing" title="Dublin Airport bombing">was bombed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Association" title="Ulster Defence Association">Ulster Defence Association</a> in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_(EI-CCW),_Dublin,_July_1993.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" data-file-height="2279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ryanair_(EI-CCW),_Dublin,_July_1993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two of the airport\'s largest operators side-by-side, a <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> <a href="/wiki/BAC_1-11" class="mw-redirect" title="BAC 1-11">BAC 1-11</a> (front) in its oldest livery, and an Aer Lingus <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> (rear) in 1993</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/BAC_1-11" class="mw-redirect" title="BAC 1-11">BAC 1-11</a> in July 1992</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a data-file-height="2291" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-ASI),_Dublin,_May_1994.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus Boeing 747 in May 1994</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-BXB),_Dublin,_May_1994.jpg" class="image"><img data-file-height="2279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aer_Lingus_(EI-BXB),_Dublin,_May_1994.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aer Lingus Boeing 737-400 and a British Airways ATR 42</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuing_in_the_1980s_and_1990s">Continuing in the 1980s and 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Continuing in the 1980s and 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 1983 Aer Lingus opened its \'Aer Lingus Commuter\' division<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> which took delivery of <a href="/wiki/Short_Brothers" title="Short Brothers">Shorts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saab_AB" title="Saab AB">Saab AB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fokker" title="Fokker">Fokker</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> aircraft to open regular daily domestic services to and from Ireland\'s smaller regional airports for the first time, as well as to serve existing routes to smaller regional airports in the United Kingdom. At various stages of its operations, flights were operated to several Irish regional airports to feed passengers into Aer Lingus\'s international network. These domestic destinations included <a href="/wiki/Cork_Airport" title="Cork Airport">Cork Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Airport" title="Shannon Airport">Shannon Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Airport" title="Kerry Airport">Kerry Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galway_Airport" title="Galway Airport">Galway Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland_West_Airport_Knock" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland West Airport Knock">Ireland West Airport Knock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterford_Airport" title="Waterford Airport">Waterford Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sligo_Airport" title="Sligo Airport">Sligo Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/City_of_Derry_Airport" title="City of Derry Airport">City of Derry Airport</a>. Aer Lingus Commuter has since been re-absorbed into the main company. The domestic routes, with the exception of Dublin-Shannon, were taken over by Aer Arann. Most of these routes have since been discontinued as the development of the motorway network in Ireland has resulted in significant reductions in travelling time by road. Aer Lingus has continued with the remaining Dublin\xe2\x80\x93UK flights.<sup id="cite_ref-80s&amp;90s_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80s&amp;90s-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1980s, major competition, especially on the Dublin\xe2\x80\x93London routes, resulted in passenger numbers swelling to 5.1 million in 1989. In the same year a new 8,650&#160;ft (2,640&#160;m) runway and a state-of-the-art air traffic control centre were opened. Dublin Airport continued to expand rapidly in the 1990s. Pier A, which had been the first extension to the old terminal building, was significantly extended. A new Pier C, complete with <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">air bridges</a>, was built and as soon as this was completed, work commenced to extend it to double its capacity. The ground floor of the original terminal building was returned to passenger service after many years to provide additional departure gates. Pier D, completed in October 2007, is a dedicated low-fares boarding area and provides 14 quick turn-around stands and departure gates; these are not served by air bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-80s&amp;90s_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80s&amp;90s-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bilateral_Air_Transport_Agreement">The Bilateral Air Transport Agreement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Bilateral Air Transport Agreement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 1993, a major milestone for the airport was the signing of a new United States \xe2\x80\x93 Ireland <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_Air_Transport_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral Air Transport Agreement">bilateral agreement</a> which allowed airlines to operate some direct transatlantic services for the first time to/from Dublin Airport instead of touching down en route at Shannon Airport on the west coast of Ireland. (Shannon had once been a major transatlantic refuelling stop for pre-jet aircraft, and this agreement was designed to protect the interests of the Shannon region when modern jets no longer required a refuelling stop and Shannon saw a fall-off in traffic.) Airlines still had to provide an equal number of flights either to or through Shannon as to Dublin. A gradual further watering down of Shannon\'s so-called \'stopover\' status came into effect in November 2006 when more direct flights to Dublin were allowed. The stopover requirement disappeared completely in 2008. At that time, airlines were allowed to fly direct to the US from Dublin without having to match these with any to/from Shannon. It was expected that this would result in a huge increase in services between Dublin and the US and Aer Lingus has identified 16 destinations that it would like to serve directly from Dublin.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With the success of Ireland\'s \'<a href="/wiki/Celtic_Tiger" title="Celtic Tiger">Celtic Tiger</a>\' economy, Dublin Airport saw growth in the 1990s and 2000s. This demand was driven by an increased demand for business travel to and from the country, together with an increase in inward tourism and a surge in demand for foreign holidays and city breaks from the <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The demand from Ireland\'s migrant workers, principally those from Eastern Europe, has resulted in a large number of new routes opening to destinations in the European Union accession states. Ireland was one of only three European Union countries (as well as the United Kingdom and Sweden) to open its borders freely to workers from the ten accession states that <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">joined the European Union in 2004</a>.\n</p><p>In 2007 the then shortest runway, 11/29, was closed and converted to an aircraft storage area.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This runway would subsequently be demolished for the construction of a second long runway parallel to 10/28. \n</p><p>The airport saw significant declines in traffic in 2009 and 2010, although since 2011 the airport has seen an increase in traffic. During 2012, this increase continued with passenger numbers growing by 1.9%. During 2013, passenger numbers at Dublin Airport were above the 20 million mark for the first time since 2009 with a 5.6% increase year on year. During 2014, this positive trend continued with an 8% increase over 2013.  As of early December 2015, passenger figures have increased by 16% compared to 2014, and the previous record of 23.46 million passengers set in 2008 has already been passed.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> 2019 was the airport\'s busiest year, recording 32.9 million passengers - an increase in passenger numbers by 4% during the year. Long-haul passenger numbers increased by 4% to almost 5.2 million, while Short-haul traffic increased by 5% to 27.7 million.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2019, Dublin Airport was chosen for the Special Achievement in Geographic Information Systems (GIS) award for its use of mapping software from ESRI Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the pandemic and its impact, the airport lost 115 routes, as in January 2021, it scheduled flights to just 85 cities, down from 200 before the crisis began.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-haul_traffic">Long-haul traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Long-haul traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As of August 2019, there are services to 31 intercontinental destinations from Dublin Airport (not including <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Dublin_Airport_Information_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dublin_Airport_Information-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Etihad Airways began operating between Dublin Airport and Abu Dhabi, and increased its capacity to 14 weekly flights in March 2010. In addition, Emirates has served Dublin from Dubai since January 2012. A total of 22 cities in North America are connected directly to Dublin Airport by seven airlines. In 2015, Ethiopian Airlines began serving Dublin from Addis Ababa, thus inaugurating the first direct air link between Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ie30918318_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ie30918318-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services_to_East_Asia">Services to East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Services to East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Government of Ireland, owner of Dublin Airport, and the Dublin Airport Authority, its operator, have long sought to connect Dublin with East Asia by direct air service.<sup id="cite_ref-ROUTES:_Ireland_and_China_seek_direct_air_link_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROUTES:_Ireland_and_China_seek_direct_air_link-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-China_air_link_in_pipeline_as_Dublin_and_Beijing_airports_become_&#39;twins&#39;_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_air_link_in_pipeline_as_Dublin_and_Beijing_airports_become_&#39;twins&#39;-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Their plans were realized in 2018 when <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> launched 4 weekly direct flights between Dublin and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>. This was followed by services to Beijing-Capital (via Edinburgh) and Shenzhen (nonstop), launched by Hainan Airlines in June 2018 and January 2019, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  In August 2019, however, Hainan Airlines withdrew from Dublin entirely.<sup id="cite_ref-Chinese_takeaway:_Hainan_axes_Dublin_route_to_Shenzhen_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese_takeaway:_Hainan_axes_Dublin_route_to_Shenzhen-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In September, due to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Hong_Kong_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019\xe2\x80\x9320 Hong Kong protests">political unrest in Hong Kong</a>, Cathay Pacific restricted its previously year-round Hong Kong route to the summer season only.<sup id="cite_ref-Cathay_Pacific\xe2\x80\x99s_Hong_Kong_to_Dublin_flights_shelved_until_end_March_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cathay_Pacific\xe2\x80\x99s_Hong_Kong_to_Dublin_flights_shelved_until_end_March-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shannon_Stopover_and_Open_Skies">Shannon Stopover and Open Skies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Shannon Stopover and Open Skies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the mid twentieth century, the Irish government introduced a rule stating that all air traffic between Ireland and the United States must transit through Shannon Airport. In return, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">United States government</a> placed a limit of four airports in the US that Aer Lingus could operate to. On 22 March 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Open_skies" class="mw-redirect" title="Open skies">Open skies</a> agreement between the US and EU was ratified. This resulted in the immediate cancellation of the long-running \'Shannon Stopover\' requirement, whereby the Irish government had insisted that 50% of all transatlantic flights between Ireland and the United States must pass through Shannon Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_border_preclearance">US border preclearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: US border preclearance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Dublin Airport is one of only two airports in Europe, and three outside the Americas, with <a href="/wiki/United_States_border_preclearance" title="United States border preclearance">United States border preclearance</a> services for US-bound passengers (the other airports are Ireland\'s Shannon Airport and one in the United Arab Emirates). Those traveling on nonstop flights to the United States complete immigration and customs procedures in Dublin prior to their departure, and are treated as domestic passengers on arrival.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Aer_Rianta_and_DAA.2FDublin_Airport_Authority"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Aer_Rianta_and_DAA/Dublin_Airport_Authority">Aer Rianta and DAA/Dublin Airport Authority</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Aer Rianta and DAA/Dublin Airport Authority">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/DAA_(Irish_company)" title="DAA (Irish company)">DAA (Irish company)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg/220px-DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg/330px-DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg/440px-DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="613" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DublinAirportAuthorityBuild.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/DAA_(Irish_company)" title="DAA (Irish company)">DAA</a> headquarters at Dublin Airport</div></div></div>\n<p>In October 2004, Aer Rianta (which is the Irish for \'Air Ways\' or \'Air Tracks\') was renamed Dublin Airport Authority plc, a result of the State Airports Act 2004. All assets and liabilities previously owned by Aer Rianta were transferred to Dublin Airport Authority. The State Airports Act 2004 also established new airport authorities at Shannon and Cork Airports. The Shannon Airport Authority and the Cork Airport Authority had separate boards of directors and were authorised under the Act to prepare business plans, which may have in time lead to their full separation from the Dublin Airport Authority. Following a decision by the Irish Government, Shannon Airport became a separate publicly owned airport on 31 December 2012.\n</p><p>In July 2013, the Dublin Airport Authority was officially renamed "<i>DAA plc</i>" by the Irish Government. The rename was principally to remove the "Dublin" and "Authority" elements of the name which were seen to have little relevance to the overall functions of DAA.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The name change announced in July 2013 took effect on 6 November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the largest gateway to Ireland, over 25 million passengers travelled through the airport in 2015, a 15% increase over the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-issuu.com_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-issuu.com-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The main contributors to the growth in traffic in 2015 were the 23 new routes launched during the year and extra capacity on 40 existing services. Both long-haul and short-haul traffic increased by 15% in 2015. A record 8.9 million people travelled between Dublin Airport and Britain during 2015, which was a 14% increase on the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-issuu.com_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-issuu.com-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>   Dublin Airport also welcomes more than one million passengers per annum from Northern Ireland and is a key international gateway for overseas visitors to Northern Ireland.,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> whose largest airport is less than a quarter the size of Dublin in terms of passenger numbers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_terminals">Passenger terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Passenger terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg/220px-Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg/330px-Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg/440px-Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_Terminal_1_Departures_Level.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1 departures level</div></div></div>\n<p>The current Terminal 1 building opened in 1972 was designed to handle five million passengers per year. The original design included a second pier which would have been identical to the current decagon-shaped boarding Pier B, but this was never built. A car park was originally located on the upper floor of the building and the access ramps are still in place but it was closed for security reasons in the 1970s and converted into offices. Terminal 1 has been regularly extended and improved over the last two decades. In October 2007, a new pier designed by <a href="/wiki/Larry_Oltmanns" title="Larry Oltmanns">Larry Oltmanns</a>, while design director of the London office of <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings_%26_Merrill" title="Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill">Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> who also designed graphics for its interior, was opened to the north of Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> This pier caters for the majority of Ryanair flights. In 2009, a new extension featuring new food and retail outlets was added to the side of Terminal 1. Terminal 1 is currently home to all airlines except Aer Lingus, American Airlines, Delta Air Lines, Emirates, Norwegian (long-haul services) and United Airlines. Pier C was demolished during the construction of Terminal 2.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg/220px-T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg/330px-T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg/440px-T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1302" data-file-height="636" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:T2Dublin_Airport-doyler79.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<p>Terminal 2 is a 75,000 m<sup>2</sup> (810,000 sq ft) terminal and pier (Pier E) which provides aircraft parking for 27 narrow body aircraft through 19 departure gates which can handle up to 15 million passengers annually.  The project was designed by <a href="/wiki/Pascall%2BWatson" title="Pascall+Watson">Pascall+Watson</a> architects and the total cost was \xe2\x82\xac600 million. <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> is the main carrier operating at Terminal 2 and since its opening have developed a hub at Dublin primarily for traffic traveling between Europe and the United States.  Terminal 2 is now the transatlantic gateway for flights to the United States as it features a <a href="/wiki/United_States_border_preclearance" title="United States border preclearance">US pre-clearance immigration facility</a> which was previously housed in Terminal 1.\n</p><p>Construction of Terminal 2 began on 1 October 2007, and it was officially opened on 19 November 2010 by the then <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> Brian Cowen T.D.  The intended purpose of Terminal 2 was to house all long-haul carriers in addition to Aer Lingus; however significant growth in US traffic has resulted in most long haul carriers flying outside the United States remaining in Terminal 1.  During the design of Terminal 2 provisions were made for an expanded check in hall and additional pier (Pier F) to cater for future growth.  Currently <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> operate from Terminal 2.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_and_security">Safety and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Safety and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>DAA has its own branch of the <a href="/wiki/Airport_Police_(Ireland)" title="Airport Police (Ireland)">Airport Police Service</a> which is mandated to provide aviation and general policing at the airport. The <a href="/wiki/Airport_Police_(Ireland)#Facilities" title="Airport Police (Ireland)">Airport Police Station</a> is centrally located on the Arrivals road between Terminals 1 and 2. The airport also has its own <a href="/wiki/Airport_Police_(Ireland)#Airport_Fire_Rescue_Service" title="Airport Police (Ireland)">Airport Fire and Rescue Service</a> which provides cover to the entire campus, its roadways and lands.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Revenue_Commissioners" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of the Revenue Commissioners">Office of the Revenue Commissioners</a> provide a customs service to both passenger and cargo terminals, while the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Agriculture,_Food_and_the_Marine" title="Department of Agriculture, Food and the Marine">Department of Agriculture</a> also has a presence in the airport. <a href="/wiki/Irish_Naturalisation_and_Immigration_Service" title="Irish Naturalisation and Immigration Service">Irish Naturalisation and Immigration Service</a> provides an Immigration service for all international passengers arriving at the airport. The <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda\xc3\xad</a> also have a small sub-station located beside the old terminal.\n</p><p>In 2016 it was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Garda_Armed_Support_Unit" title="Garda Armed Support Unit">Garda Armed Support Units</a> (ASU) would be deployed overtly to patrol Dublin Airport and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Port" title="Dublin Port">Dublin Port</a> full-time on foot inside terminal buildings and via vehicles outside and surrounding the perimeter to counter the rising threat of terrorist attacks in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The decision was made as a direct result of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">2016 Brussels bombings</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance_facilities">Maintenance facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Maintenance facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Aer Lingus, Ryanair, <a href="/wiki/CityJet" title="CityJet">CityJet</a>, Eirtech and Dublin Aerospace have aircraft maintenance hangars and facilities at Dublin Airport. In 2010 <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> announced a new maintenance hangar which will handle the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-200">Airbus A330-200</a> which the airline uses on their route from Abu Dhabi to Dublin. In time the airline will allow other airlines to use this facility.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_developments">Airport developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Airport developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%94%D1%8A%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD_1447249811_0376745dc3_o.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" (centre, now replaced by Terminal 2) clearly visible with Cargo ramp and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> Maintenance facilities.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_air_traffic_control_complex">New air traffic control complex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: New air traffic control complex">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Construction is currently under way on a new air traffic control complex and <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a> which will replace the existing structure. The new facility has been designed by <a href="/wiki/Scott_Tallon_Walker" title="Scott Tallon Walker">Scott Tallon Walker</a> architects. A planning application was submitted in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The new control tower will be 87.7&#160;m (288&#160;ft) in height. The new control tower is necessary because the construction of the future parallel runway will obstruct visibility of certain parts of the airport from the existing control tower.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_runway">New runway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: New runway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A new runway measuring 3,110&#160;m (10,203&#160;ft) is currently under construction parallel to the existing runway 10R/28L, which opened (as runway 10/28) in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Planning_permission" title="Planning permission">Planning permission</a> for the runway was originally granted in August 2007, with 31 planning conditions attached.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The new runway will run parallel to the north of runway 10R/28L and allow the airport to accommodate 30 million passengers per annum once in operation, and it will be 3,110&#160;m (10,203&#160;ft) long.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In March 2009 the DAA announced in a proposal for consultation that the new runway may be built to a length of 3,660&#160;m (12,008&#160;ft) following consultation with potential long-haul carriers. A runway of this length would allow direct flights from Dublin to the Far East.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The runway was expected to cost in the region of \xe2\x82\xac300 million.\n</p><p>In the meantime, the company has invested heavily in extending aprons and creating rapid exit <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiways</a> to derive maximum efficiency from the existing main runway. Runway 16/34 is often used during the day as a taxiway for aircraft utilizing runway 10R/28L. 16/34 is often used in the evening, depending on airport construction.\n</p><p>After a delay of several years due to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007-2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007-2010">global financial crisis</a> and predictions of falling consumer demand, it was announced in April 2016 that the new runway would start construction in 2017 and to be completed by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>On 8 October 2020, the existing runway 10/28 was redesignated as 10R/28L in anticipation of the new runway becoming 10L/28R.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Airport">Maastricht</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_numbers">Passenger numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Passenger numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Passenger numbers at Dublin Airport increased every year during the 10 years between 1998 and 2008, from around 11.6 million to over 23.4 million. Passenger numbers fell however during the subsequent two years to around 18.4 million in 2010, with a small increase to 18.7 million in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-daa11_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daa11-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and 19.1 million in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-daa12_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daa12-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> then 2013 saw a significant increase of 5.6% to 20.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-DAA2013_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DAA2013-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, passenger numbers increased by almost 8% to over 21.7 million.<sup id="cite_ref-daa2015_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daa2015-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Traffic growth of over 15% during 2015 resulted in passenger numbers exceeding 25 million for the first time.  The previous record of 23.46 million (set in 2008) was exceeded during the first week of December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-DAA2015_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DAA2015-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Graph">Graph</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Graph">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<style class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Outside_Dublin_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Outside_Dublin_Airport.jpg/440px-Outside_Dublin_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Outside_Dublin_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outside the airport</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_buses,_Mercedes-Benz_Citaro_G_C1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dublin_Airport_buses%2C_Mercedes-Benz_Citaro_G_C1.jpg/220px-Dublin_Airport_buses%2C_Mercedes-Benz_Citaro_G_C1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" data-file-height="1883" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Airport_buses,_Mercedes-Benz_Citaro_G_C1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport bus</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Bus_line_16,_Dublin_Airport_(2019).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg/220px-Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg/330px-Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg/440px-Dublin_Bus_line_16%2C_Dublin_Airport_%282019%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin_Bus_line_16,_Dublin_Airport_(2019).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dublin buses serving the airport</div></div></div>\n<p>Dublin Airport is located just off the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway_(Republic_of_Ireland)" title="M1 motorway (Republic of Ireland)">M1</a> and the <a href="/wiki/M50_motorway_(Ireland)" title="M50 motorway (Ireland)">M50</a> 10&#160;km (6.2&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> north from the city centre and 2&#160;km (1.2&#160;mi) south of the town of Swords. The airport is approximately 210 kilometres (130&#160;mi) away from both <a href="/wiki/Limerick" title="Limerick">Limerick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a> and 266 kilometres (165&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>. <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> is around 158 kilometres (98&#160;mi) away. There is no rail link to Dublin city centre, and the public transport options to the city are taxis, buses and private transport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_services">Bus services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bus services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Dublin Airport is served by a large network of bus and coach routes, serving both the wider Dublin area and intercity links to the rest of Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> More than 700 buses a day service Dublin Airport. In Dublin city, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Bus" title="Dublin Bus">Dublin Bus</a> is the main provider of transport to and from the airport operating Airlink Express routes 747 and 757 to the city centre terminus of <a href="/wiki/Bus%C3%A1ras" title="Bus\xc3\xa1ras">Bus\xc3\xa1ras</a> and the railway stations of <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Connolly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Connolly railway station">Dublin Connolly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Heuston_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Heuston railway station">Dublin Heuston</a>, as well as to Merrion Square and Camden Street, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Dublin Bus and <a href="/wiki/Go-Ahead_Ireland" title="Go-Ahead Ireland">Go-Ahead Ireland</a> run local stopping services that serve such residential areas as <a href="/wiki/Santry" title="Santry">Santry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swords,_Dublin" title="Swords, Dublin">Swords</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rathfarnham" title="Rathfarnham">Rathfarnham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sutton,_Dublin" title="Sutton, Dublin">Sutton</a>, Malahide, <a href="/wiki/Beaumont,_Dublin" title="Beaumont, Dublin">Beaumont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold%27s_Cross" title="Harold&#39;s Cross">Harold\'s Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drumcondra,_Dublin" title="Drumcondra, Dublin">Drumcondra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balbriggan" title="Balbriggan">Balbriggan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skerries,_Dublin" title="Skerries, Dublin">Skerries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rush,_Dublin" title="Rush, Dublin">Rush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portmarnock" title="Portmarnock">Portmarnock</a>, with routes 16, 33A, 41, 41B and 102.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Aircoach" title="Aircoach">Aircoach</a> offers a number of coach services from the Airport to the Dublin area, serving both the city centre and surrounding areas including <a href="/wiki/Donnybrook,_Dublin" title="Donnybrook, Dublin">Donnybrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopardstown" title="Leopardstown">Leopardstown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandyford" title="Sandyford">Sandyford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalkey" title="Dalkey">Dalkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greystones" title="Greystones">Greystones</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bray,_County_Wicklow" title="Bray, County Wicklow">Bray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blackrock,_Dublin" title="Blackrock, Dublin">Blackrock</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BAn_Laoghaire" title="D\xc3\xban Laoghaire">D\xc3\xban Laoghaire</a> <a href="/wiki/Killiney" title="Killiney">Killiney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandymount" title="Sandymount">Sandymount</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dublin Coach links <a href="/wiki/Dundrum,_Dublin" title="Dundrum, Dublin">Dundrum</a> and Red Cow <a href="/wiki/Luas" title="Luas">Luas</a> to Dublin Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At a national level, <a href="/wiki/Bus_%C3%89ireann#Expressway" title="Bus \xc3\x89ireann">Expressway</a> offers a large number of routes from Dublin Airport to 18 destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limerick" title="Limerick">Limerick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterford" title="Waterford">Waterford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drogheda" title="Drogheda">Drogheda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navan" title="Navan">Navan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dundalk" title="Dundalk">Dundalk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Bus \xc3\x89ireann and <a href="/wiki/Ulsterbus" title="Ulsterbus">Ulsterbus Goldline</a> jointly offer cross-border bus services, namely X1/X2 to Belfast. Translink solely operate services X3/X4 to <a href="/wiki/Derry" title="Derry">Derry</a> via either <a href="/wiki/Monaghan" title="Monaghan">Monaghan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Omagh" title="Omagh">Omagh</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Armagh" title="Armagh">Armagh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cookstown" title="Cookstown">Cookstown</a> respectively.\n</p><p>Citylink and Gobus offer services to Galway while \xc3\x89irebus and <a href="/wiki/JJ_Kavanagh_and_Sons" title="JJ Kavanagh and Sons">JJ Kavanagh</a> operate regular services to Limerick, <a href="/wiki/Kilkenny" title="Kilkenny">Kilkenny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Waterford" title="Waterford">Waterford</a>. Wexfordbus connects the airport with Wexford, and John McGinley Coaches also connects the airport with <a href="/wiki/Donegal_(town)" title="Donegal (town)">Donegal</a> ending in <a href="/wiki/Annagry" title="Annagry">Annagry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Taxis are available at taxi ranks located directly outside of Terminal 1 and Terminal 2.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There is no direct rail connection to Dublin Airport. However, <i><a href="/wiki/Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann" title="Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann">Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann</a></i> (Irish Rail) provide suburban and <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann)" title="InterCity (Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann)">intercity</a> railway services from <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Connolly" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Connolly">Dublin Connolly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Heuston" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Heuston">Dublin Heuston</a> railway stations, and there are regular bus services from both stations to the airport. Some city bus services serve <a href="/wiki/Drumcondra_railway_station" title="Drumcondra railway station">Drumcondra</a> suburban railway station, which is on the Connolly to Maynooth railway line while the 102 route connects Dublin Airport to Sutton <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dublin Area Rapid Transit">DART</a> station. Bus services to Bus\xc3\xa1ras/Dublin Connolly and Dublin Heuston railway stations connect with the <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(Luas)" title="Red Line (Luas)">Luas Red Line</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_rail_link">Proposed rail link</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Proposed rail link">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>For many years, it was expected that Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann would extend the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dublin Area Rapid Transit">Dublin Area Rapid Transit (DART)</a> to serve the airport. These plans were replaced with a proposal for an underground metro line, which would run from the city centre to <a href="/wiki/Swords,_Dublin" title="Swords, Dublin">Swords</a> via the airport. The route for the line, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Metro#Metro_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Metro">Metro North</a>, was announced in October 2006 and was proposed to connect with several other modes of transport. In 2011, it was announced that the Metro North plan would be deferred due to a lack of funding.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> As of March 2018, an updated plan suggested that the Metro line might "be open to the public from 2027" but that the details, line, route and timelines were all "subject to change as the final designs haven\'t been confirmed".<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dublin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Airport_Police_(Ireland)" title="Airport Police (Ireland)">Airport Police (Ireland)</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span
